Because of my sensitive skin I usually only shave 2 to 3 times a week and I would say the blades dull noticeably after 5 shaves but continue to work well for about 10-12 shaves.  So if you only shave twice a week these blades will last you 5 weeks.  Compared to the regular fusion I would say these blades last maybe a shave or 2 longer, but it&#x27;s really a toss up.&lt;br /&gt;&lt;br /&gt;In conclusion I highly recommend Gillette Fusion razors in general for a close and comfortable shave.  When switching between the regular Fusion and the Fusion Proglide Power however I do not think the cartridges are worth the additional cost.  If you have extremely sensitive skin it may be worth a try, but if you are getting the shave you want from the Gillette Fusion, you will probably not notice an improvement either.ar Fusion and the Fusion Proglide Power however I do not think the cartridges are worth the additional cost.     <li> First up, my history. When I first started shaving, I used a disposable manual razor. Twice. After that, realizing shaving wasn&#x27;t something one could usually get out of by choice, I bought an electric razor, of the rotary type. When the Gillette Mach 3 was introduced, I got that to keep for a backup, or for a closer shave for important events, concerts, shows, etc. Eventually I upgraded my rotary razor to a Braun Pulsonic (expensive) razor. Soon after, I tried the Gillette Fusion Power, to see how it compared. Lets just say it compared just enough to be actually worth comparing. This again went into the cabinet as a special occasional razor. About three months ago, as the cartridge in my Braun Pulsonic was aging beyond it&#x27;s recommended life cycle and the shave was getting less close, and more painful, I decided to try the Gillette Proglides cartridges. I used them on my Gillette Fusion Power handle, since it&#x27;s basically the same as the Proglide handle.&lt;br /&gt;&lt;br /&gt;Here was my experience with not one but four separate cartridges:&lt;br /&gt;&lt;br /&gt;I decided to shave at roughly the same time every day, just to get a real good idea of how it performed in relation to my electric. I also shaved the day prior, with my electric.&lt;br /&gt;The very first shave was very smooth and close, with no tug and pull, just as advertised. I was surprised, but pleased. It did tend to nick up my face pretty bad, but the blades were sharp enough so it didn&#x27;t affect comfort. I shave well in advance of leaving home, so this wouldn&#x27;t have been a big deal. The second and subsequent shaves were dramatically different from the first one. All were painful, rough, uneven, and frankly not all that close. I was close to just heading back to the Pulsonic with two year (plus) old cartridge, but I decided to stick it out. As the strip of lubricant wore down significantly, the comfort of the shave improved. It wasn&#x27;t as close, but it was almost, if not as comfortable as the first. This lasted until the strip was nearly gone, and it was clearly time to replace.&lt;br /&gt;I decided at that point to return to my Pulsonic, and just buy the new cartridge, as it had served me well for two years on one cartridge.&lt;br /&gt;&lt;br /&gt;A few weeks later, I had an interview, so I bought a three cartridge set of the Proglide cartridges. I decided that after I used the one for the interview, I would use the other two to do a slightly different test.&lt;br /&gt;&lt;br /&gt;With the final two cartridges, I decided to wait varying periods of time between shaves, so the stubble would be a different length each time.&lt;br /&gt;Overall, the results were the same as the first time, with a few differences. Any shave of stubble that was between two days and five days old was much more comfortable and close than it would have been at the same point in the cartridge life cycle with shorter stubble. The longest stubble, which was about six days growth, resulted in a shave that was less close, but as comfortable as the other longer-stubble shaves.&lt;br /&gt;&lt;br /&gt;I don&#x27;t know whether my rate of stubble growth is typical or atypical, but I can grow a nice goatee in about a week.&lt;br /&gt;&lt;br /&gt;Overall, I think that Gillette is going in the right direction, but they need to strike a finer balance between shave quality, and longevity of blades in order to make these worthwhile.&lt;br /&gt;&lt;br /&gt;After all the hype (which I tried to ignore, but who can, really?) I was expecting something different, and much improved. Frankly, even the few times when I turn to a manual razor, I would probably turn to the old Fusion, just because I didn&#x27;t have as many guessing games. It worked until it stopped, which was just before the color from the strip was gone. Even for someone who shaves primarily with a manual razor, unless they have money to blow, I wouldn&#x27;t recommend the Proglide.&lt;br /&gt;&lt;br /&gt;Overall, my opinion is that this is a debatable improvement over the previous generation, and that it was so far over-hyped that it created false expectations. Had it notbeen hyped so much as a dramatic improvement, I might have given it four stars, but that type of advertising really irks me.&lt;br /&gt;&lt;br /&gt;NOTE: This was my experience with the product, and since this sort of product depends a lot on individual faces, hair, shaving habits, etc., it&#x27;s not good to draw a conclusion based solely on a few other reviews. In addition, different people expect different things from a razor. I prefer a balance of longevity, comfort and closeness, while others prefer one over the others. My opinion is: if you&#x27;re an owner of a Fusion handle, you can always get a small pack of the Proglide cartridges and try them out. They may well work differently for you.been hyped so much as a dramatic improvement, I might have given it four stars, but that type of advertising really irks me.&lt;br /&gt;&lt;br /&gt;NOTE: This was my experience with the product, and since this sort of product depends a lot on individual faces, hair, shaving habits, etc., it&#x27;s not good to draw a conclusion based solely on a few other reviews. In addition, different people expect different things from a razor. I prefer a balance of longevity, comfort and closeness, while others prefer one over the others. My opinion is: if you&#x27;re an owner of a Fusion handle, you can always get a small pack of the Proglide cartridges and try them out. They may well work differently for you.</li>

    <li> I had a beard for 37 years but shaved it off just before turning 60.  I&#x27;ve been all around the shaving block in the past 10 mos and have spent alot of money trying tons of different shaving solutions for pre,during, and post shave and here&#x27;s what I have come up with:  Fusion Proglide Power cartridges, manual razor, Africa&#x27;s Best Herbal Oil ($2 for 8oz at Walmart), keep the razor (cartridge side down) covered in mineral oil between shaves.  If the blades seem to &amp;#34;tug&amp;#34; a little, just strop them on your wet arm in the shower about 10 or 15 times (i.e. opposite direction of shaving).&lt;br /&gt;&lt;br /&gt;This cartridge is AWESOME but expensive.  The subscribe and save price is okay.  But if you will keep the blades covered in mineral oil between shaves, they will last for months making them quite a bit cheaper PER SHAVE than old fashioned double-edge safety razor blades.&lt;br /&gt;The procedure I&#x27;ve settled on (after watching hours of youtube and reading lots of articles) is to clean them under high pressure hot water in the sink, both sides.  Shake dry and spray with alcohol.  Blow dry on hot, stick cartridge head down (handle up) in a container of mineral oil (enough to cover the cartridge).  It actually does work.  If you feel a tug of discomfort (I do about ever 10 shaves) then strop it against your arm about 15 times.  The cartridge will go on and on when combined with the storing oil AND the shaving oil (Africa&#x27;s Best Herbal).&lt;br /&gt;&lt;br /&gt;Shaving with oil and water and nothing else is the way to go.  I typically use 4 drops for my face and neck.  Then during the shave I let the water hit my face once in a while.  I don&#x27;t have a problem with stubble clogging the blades for two reasons:  The mineral oil soak dislodges any left over stubble, and the Fusion cartridge is open from the back.  So during the shower I allow the shower water to hit the back of the cartridge and combined with the oil it just pushes out stubble.  I find I don&#x27;t have to rinse very often during the shave.  Also with oil and cartridge you can just keep shaving till you&#x27;&#x27;re done.  No 2nd pass or 3rd pass, no reapplying oil or anything.  Just let the water hit your face a couple times during the shave.  Just keep shaving till all is clean.  Its SO NICE and SO FAST.  Try it 3 times in a row and you may just get hooked!     <li> For my &amp;#34;field test,&amp;#34; I used this product with a ProGlide razor body. I washed my face with cool water, left my face wet, then applied a smooth layer of the Proglide gel. Then the shave quality seems to drop quickly to a somewhat labored effort (multiple passes over the same locations).  But the outcome is still comfortable and smooth.  After the aforementioned 15-20 uses, razor burn begins to increase and smoothness begins to suffer with my wiry hairs not getting completely shaved.  Throughout the period of use, cleaning has been simple under a good stream of water.&lt;br /&gt;&lt;br /&gt;My experiences with these blades include use of various name-brand canned shaving creams (some better than others), soap only, hair conditioner only, premium skin lotion only, and professional shaving soap.     <li> As a man with sensitive skin, I&#x27;m very choosey when it comes to my razors.  I prefer a close shave, and that&#x27;s hard to get every day without getting razorburn.  I used to space out my shaves, only because I disliked the constant and inevitable razorburn that came with it.&lt;br /&gt;&lt;br /&gt;Enter Gillette Fusion ProGlide Power.  I received this razor free through a program run by Gillette, and I have to say, this lives up to the expectations and the hype that Gillette has poured into Fusion ProGlide over the years.  A lot of people like to make fun of the increasing number of blades in today&#x27;s razors, but Gillette has been rocking 5 blades for years now, and just improved the Fusion formula with ProGlide.  Full disclosure: I am already a huge fan of the original ProGlide razor,  so I&#x27;m viewing this from the perspective of both the original and the Power.  There are subtle differences in the cartridges, and for now, I&#x27;m going to focus purely on the blades.&lt;br /&gt;&lt;br /&gt;Both the ProGlide and ProGlide Power have much in common, but they hold some big distinctions from other razors on the market, including Gillette&#x27;s own.  I have experience with Bic disposable two-blade razors (butchered my face), Gillette Mach3 (left me with horrible razorburn), Schick Quattro (clogged to unusability after a few uses, or one shaggy shave), and Gillette Fusion (good shave, but occasional tug and pull).  The ProGlide razors have none of those issues.  The first time I used a ProGlide razor, I couldn&#x27;t even believe I was shaving. I couldn&#x27;t feel it at all!  Today, my face has become more accustomed to the razor, but here are things you can expect from it:&lt;br /&gt;- No tug and pull&lt;br /&gt;- Easy to rinse out (no clogs!)&lt;br /&gt;- Little to no razorburn (with the right cream/gel)&lt;br /&gt;- An extremely close shave&lt;br /&gt;&lt;br /&gt;The MicroComb is the big difference between the ProGlide and the ProGlide Power.  Your choice should solely depend upon whether or not you intend to use the Power feature.  I haven&#x27;t used it enough yet to give it a comprehensive in-depth analysis, but I will say one thing: buy for what you will use, and stick with it, because they&#x27;re designed to be used based on that feature.  The MicroComb on the ProGlide Power is smaller, likely because the vibration pulls the hair into a smaller, metal comb parallel to the blades to prep the hair.  If you&#x27;re not using the Power feature, you&#x27;re actually paying more for an inferior razor.  Your shave may still be simple, but it likely won&#x27;t be as close or smooth.&lt;br /&gt;&lt;br /&gt;Other, smaller differences... The lubricating strip is a different color (Power &#x3D; green, original &#x3D; blue), which doesn&#x27;t mean much, but they seem to have a slightly different texture.  I haven&#x27;t see this make much difference.  The surface of the trimmer blade on the back of the Power seems ever-so-slightly larger, but I haven&#x27;t seen it make much of a difference in practice either.&lt;br /&gt;&lt;br /&gt;Are you still looking for downsides to this razor?  I honestly tried to find some, and nothing came up.  Everything about it works great.  I really wish I could provide a better overview of the vibration feature, but that will have to wait until I&#x27;ve had more time to evaluate it.&lt;br /&gt;&lt;br /&gt;If you have a Fusion, should you upgrade to a ProGlide?  YES. World of difference.  It is totally worth it.  Give it a try once and see for yourself.  If you&#x27;re using another brand, should you switch?  I&#x27;ve tried many others, and so far, I haven&#x27;t seen anything that comes close.  It&#x27;s worth a try.  Chances are, you won&#x27;t go back.&lt;br /&gt;&lt;br /&gt;UPDATE: I&#x27;ve since had a chance to try the vibration feature.  When I first heard of the vibrating feature, I didn&#x27;t think much of it.  In fact, I used the vibrating feature on the original Fusion and it did nothing for me, which caused me to label it gimmick.  Well, Gillette must&#x27;ve gone back to the drawing board, because this new power razor is a real treat.  To keep it simple, if you&#x27;re looking for the absolute closest shave with a multi-blade razor, here it is.&lt;br /&gt;&lt;br /&gt;I&#x27;ve always had trouble in rougher spots, particularly my neck.  No matter which way I shave, I never really get a smooth feel because the hair is so coarse, and it&#x27;s hard to maneuver in that position.  Yet, this razor does MUCH better than its non-power cousin.  Here&#x27;s the magic: the micropulses from the battery-powered handle help guide the hairs into the microcomb that line the bottom of the cartridge, which then feed to the blades and cut the hair as close to the skin as possible.  What&#x27;s even more incredible that my now even closer shave adds no additional irritation... in fact, it seems to have lessened the irritation!  If you&#x27;re looking for an even smoother and more comfortable shave than you already get with the manual ProGlide, you&#x27;ve found your answer.&lt;br /&gt;&lt;br /&gt;The handle itself, because of the battery and motor, has considerable size and heft compared to its non-powered cousin.  I actually find it easier to grip when approaching those hard-to-reach spots.  It might be a little hard to adjust to, expecially if you&#x27;ve been using a thinner handle for a long time, but it doesn&#x27;t make the task any more cumbersome.&lt;br /&gt;&lt;br /&gt;There is one big drawback to the micropulses.  The vibration makes it hard to tell where you&#x27;re making contact with your skin, and as a result, you might miss a few spots if you rely more on feel, rather than sight, like I do when I shave.  The pulses are strong enough that you can feel the effects in a radius around where the razor is actually shaving.  You need to pay very close attention to ensure you don&#x27;t miss a spot.  I have done this several times, and originally attributed it to my own laziness, but given that this doesn&#x27;t happen to me with the manual razor, I unfortunately have to say that this razor, though it requires less effort for that close shave, requires more effort for a COMPLETE SHAVE.&lt;br /&gt;&lt;br /&gt;Overall: If you want to closest shave possible, the vibration is not a gimmick.  It does the job.  Men with a particularly heavy beard will find no better option.  If you don&#x27;t have any coarse spots, you may still find this a bit smoother, but you might not see a concrete benefit outside of comfort, and it might be easier to hit every inch of your face otherwise.  Still five stars, with the caveat that you need to use more care to ensure you haven&#x27;t missed anything.lti-blade razor, here it is.&lt;br /&gt;&lt;br /&gt;I&#x27;ve always had trouble in rougher spots, particularly my neck. It seemed difficult to cut myself, which is both good/great in terms of safety, but we are talking about a razor here, a dangerous, sharp tool for chiseling facial masterpieces.&lt;br /&gt;&lt;br /&gt;I found it difficult to edge and shape straight lines with the bulkiness of the cartridges edges. The blades don&#x27;t run to the edges, so I was just scraping plastic against my face, which wasn&#x27;t cleaning up stubble precisely. The size of the cartridge was big, so the area on my cheek was hard to shape because the cartridge was intruding in my eye space, which was scary. The thought of a razor blade in the eye is frightening. So I tried a vertical motion instead of a horizontal one, it did okay, but the swiveling/pivoting feature had me making several passes since the blades just weren&#x27;t taking the hair right out.&lt;br /&gt;&lt;br /&gt;The lotion strip actually works on this cartridge. I&#x27;ve used mach 3&#x27;s and others like it in the past and always wondered what purpose these \\&quot;moisturizing strips\\&quot; actually served. However, because of past failures of this feature, it seems hardly important, if not completely insignificant. Most razor uses don&#x27;t dry shave like I do, meaning that shaving cream and after shave moisturizers are usually in the mix, so what&#x27;s the point?&lt;br /&gt;&lt;br /&gt;I agree with some other reviewers that their blades should be replaced with sharper stronger ones. The pivoting action makes you really push down hard to get close shaves, which seems counter intuitive. I want the first pass to cut some hairs, not have me press down so hard that I feel like I&#x27;m going to split my skin open, even then, it still doesn&#x27;t.&lt;br /&gt;&lt;br /&gt;However, for full face shaves and clearing out beard real estate, this razor might be excellent and safe, but I haven&#x27;t done that in years.     <li> I shaved with a Mach 3 handle/blade for something like 10+ years.  At some point I finally made the decision to make a leap to something new, and I researched a bit and decided on the Fusion Proglide Power over the Fusion.  I went with the Power option, even though I was skeptical at first, but I figured if I didn&#x27;t want it, I could simply not use it, and I&#x27;d have a manual razor.&lt;br /&gt;&lt;br /&gt;Well, a few years later, my skin and complexion have improved even further, and I get a killer smooth shave every single time.  It really does guide the hair and the power function greatly reduces drag.  I have a super thick beard (have since age 14); with proper shaving technique and this blade (I do use the Fusion Proglide *Power* blades), my face looks incredibly clear and feels smooth as a baby&#x27;s butt.&lt;br /&gt;&lt;br /&gt;I used to have broken out skin pretty badly when I first started shaving; I since have developed a routine and constantly get compliments on my skin.  Here&#x27;s what I do:&lt;br /&gt;&lt;br /&gt;After the morning shower, I begin by splashing my face/beard with warm/hot water repeatedly, to soak and expand the hair.  Then I APPLY [[ASIN:B001E6Q652 Kiss My Face Fragrance Free Moisture Shave, 11-Ounce Pumps (Pack of 4)]] AGAINST the grain (this makes the hairs stand up a bit and easier to guide into the blade); swirl it all over the face to make the hair stand up.&lt;br /&gt;&lt;br /&gt;Then SHAVE WITH THE GRAIN, then across the grain at a 90 degree angle; in other words, you shave from the far side of your cheek towards your mouth, horizontally; this is a common technique used in barber shops, etc, that gives you the smoothness of shaving AGAINST the grain, without the irritation/bleeding involved in doing so (particularly if you have a thick beard; mine is so thick that if I were to shave directly against the grain I would nearly bleed to death).&lt;br /&gt;&lt;br /&gt;Then lightly towel off (don&#x27;t wash off; this product has healthy oils that should be left in small quantities in the skin). to remove excess shaving cream and hair.&lt;br /&gt;&lt;br /&gt;Lastly, apply [[ASIN:B00CCAW84W Tend Skin Refillable Roll-On System]] or [[ASIN:B0007RNBPM Tend Skin The Skin Care Solution]] (I prefer the roll-on); this has been the single greatest lifesaver product for my neck in my life.  I&#x27;ve used it, every day to other day, for the past 17 years, literally!  Before this product, I tried EVERYTHING, including fancy ultra expensive products from the cosmetics department at a department store at the mall (a guy called out \\&quot;do you have trouble with having irritation?!\\&quot; and got my attention...  sold me $100+ of stuff but the stuff was junk).  Then I read about Tend Skin in a Men&#x27;s Health magazine and my whole life changed; my sensitive skin + heavy beard &#x3D; irritated neck problem was gone.  This product is definitely the magic ingredient.&lt;br /&gt;&lt;br /&gt;That said, Fusion Proglide Power is a big part of the process, and in my experience, is the smoothest and least irritating razor I have used to date.  I also find that the blades last longer than the Mach 3 blades did (they were truly pathetic); so I am spending less on them overall.
